Round 10 Feature Match: Not So Mystic After All - Adam Cai vs. Aaron Clay
-------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

Aaron Clay is a level 1 DCI Judge. Adam Cai is a regular on the StarCityGames Open Circuit. Both players are competing with one of the best colors in the format: white. However Adam's list is lacking something quite interesting: he opted to not run [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), the format's perennial tutor of equipment!


Both players discussed the previous day's matches as they shuffled up and began to battle. This early in the morning things tend to be pretty relaxed.


### Game 1


Adam was on the play, which meant it was a little less painful for Aaron that he had to go down to six cards. Adam led with a [Horizon Canopy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Horizon+Canopy) into a [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) while Aaron led with a [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta). After a [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for zero from Adam, Aaron promptly responded with a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce). This meant Adam simply had to play a second Hierarch and pass.


Aaron played a [Tower of the Magistrate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tower+of+the+Magistrate), which was quickly met with a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) from Adam. Aaron chose to [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) in response, but the land was still destined for the grumper. Adam cast a [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman), and with Aaron tapped out it would resolve. Adam swung in for two with an exalted Hierarch and shipped the turn.


With the initiative now his, Aaron played a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), seeking up a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) to meet Adam's growing forces. With only two mana to his name, he was forced to pass back the turn. Adam untapped, cast a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on the Mystic, and promptly played a [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage). This meant that his swing with the [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) was for a massive five damage!


Although composed of only tiny creatures, Adam's army was growing sizeable. Aaron was resigned to simply play a land and pass. Adam went into the tank. He played a forest then attacked for another five with his [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage). Adam searched out a land, dropping to 12 life, then cast a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) targeting his [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). Aaron chose to chump block the cat, then Adam added a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) to his team. Aaron needed an answer, and fast!



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Adam%20Cai.JPG)
*Adam Cai*

Aaron played a [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) followed by a second [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), this time searching out an [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte). With a mere two mana free, he didn't hesitate to cast the Jitte and pass the turn. With Aaron tapped out, this was Adam's chance. He cast a second [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) on Aaron's second [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), before going into the tank. Adam activated his Knight, fetching out a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to kill Aaron's only white source in a [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra). This momentarily left Adam with zero lands, relying on two [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch)s, before playing a [Windswept Heath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Windswept+Heath) and attacking with his 5/5 [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman). This would drop Aaron to eight life.


Aaron was able to play a [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) on his next turn, making Adam's [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) all for naught. Aaron mainphased a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) targeting an irrelevant [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce), then cracked his fetch land. He equipped the Jitte, but was still staring down an unimpressed [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage) that wasted no time in dispatching the legendary equipment. Adam fetched out a land as well, and the life totals were seven to 14 in Adam's favor.


Adam drew for his turn and played a [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas). He then attacked with his now 4/4 [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) and Aaron dropped to three life with no blocks. Adam took this opportunity to [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for three mana, searching out a *second* [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). He then activated the first Knight, found a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), and destroyed Aaron's Factory.


"It's looking pretty good for you over there," Aaron remarked.


He looked at his draw for the turn then packed them up.


Adam Cai 1, Aaron Clay 0


### Game 2


Both players joked about the format, and how good [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) is while they shuffled one another's decks.


Aaron chose to leads off this game, and fortunately had a keepable hand. He led with a [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn) while Adam played a Windswept heath, cracked it, and played a [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch). Unfortunately for Adam, Aaron took his turn and laid another dreaded [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). A [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) once more found its way to Aaron's hand and he gave the turn to Adam.


Adam now had the opportunity to cast a [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage) and took it. He then swung in for two with his exalted Hierarch and passed the turn. Aaron played a land and passed the turn, presenting Adam with the threat of three untapped lands and an active [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). Adam played a [Maze of Ith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+of+Ith) then attacked with his Pridemage before Aaron used a [Path to Exile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Path+to+Exile) on it. It now looked like the coast was clear for Adam's [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) to run rampant. Aaron fetched out a [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra) with his [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) and put a surprising [Sword of Body and Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Body+and+Mind) into play at the end of Adam's turn.


Aaron equipped the [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) and attacked; and much to Adam's dismay, it would connect. Aaron now had a wolf while Adam's library was ten cards lighter. At the end of Aaron's turn, Adam chose to cast a [Scryb Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scryb+Ranger). Adam played a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) and immediately used it on Aaron's [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra). Adam attacked for two with his [Scryb Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scryb+Ranger), putting Aaron to 14 life before casting a [Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Green+Sun%27s+Zenith) for three. Once more a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) would come down, and threaten to search out a [Maze of Ith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maze+of+Ith) to nullify the [Sword of Body and Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Body+and+Mind) Aaron was wielding.


Aaron attacked again bringing Adam down to 12 life while getting a second Wolf and removing ten more cards. Aaron had the [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) for the Knight, but immediately lamented his misplay by letting Adam gain an enormous twelve life! Adam untapped, played a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), and got rid of another of Aaron's [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra)s. He then played a Scavenging Ooze that had a *lot* of options to feast on. Another attack from Aaron brought Adam to a less threatening 21 life, but his deck was shrinking by the turn.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Aaron%20Clay.JPG)
*Aaron Clay*

Adam chose to exile some [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster targets in Aaron's graveyard, but during his draw step a [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) targeting Adam would prove to make all information known. Adam played a [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes), but with Aaron now controlling a flier, it might not matter. Adam had a mere thirteen cards in his library as the two players decided to shuffle up and go to game three!


Adam Cai 1, Aaron Clay 1


### Game 3


"Do you like [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) in there?" Aaron asked, as the two players prepared for game three.


"Oh yeah," Cai responded confidently.


Aaron was going to Paris once more, while Adam was content with his opener. With a mere six minutes left on the clock, would this match end in a draw? Adam led off with a [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes) and quickly passed the turn.


In a similarly hasty fashion, Aaron played a [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra) then removed the Mother with a [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares). Adam kept the beats coming with a turn two [Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben), which would threaten to put the vice grips on Aaron. Aaron searched out a second land to play his [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), once more getting a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull). It was a land and an attack from Adam before he cast a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary).


Aaron played a [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) and passed the turn. Adam played his forth land - a possible record number - then floated a green mana before sacrificing it to [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary). He found a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) with the intent to get rid of Aaron's [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra). In response, Aaron chose to [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), but he forgot that it would cost him two mana instead of one. He floated a blue mana and Adam played a Scavenging Ooze. Aaron was now at 14 life after an attack and it was his turn. With a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) of his own, he passed the turn back with little action. Adam used his [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to get rid of Aaron's Factory and Aaron responded with a [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster. He chump blocked the Knight, and dropped down to 11 life. Without a third land to his name, things were looking grim for Aaron. Adam attacked for another four damage, dropping Aaron to seven life, but with Adam threatening nine power on board it was time for Aaron to pack it up!


Adam Cai 2, Aaron Clay 1




Sunday, 11:18 a.m. – Deck Tech: GW Aggro with Adam Cai
------------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

While GW Aggro might be one of the runaway archetypes in Legacy this weekend, as Adam Cai marks his return to the country, he's playing something a little bit different. With a record of 9-1 he's gotta be doing something right, so let's check out what he has in store!

[Horizon Canopy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BHorizon%5D+%5BCanopy%5D)


1
[Wooded Foothills](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BWooded%5D+%5BFoothills%5D)


1
[Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMisty%5D+%5BRainforest%5D)


4
[Windswept Heath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BWindswept%5D+%5BHeath%5D)


1
[Elesh Norn, Grand Cenobite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BElesh%5D+%5BNorn,%5D+%5BGrand%5D+%5BCenobite%5D)


4
[Green Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BGreen%5D+%5BSun%5D+%5BZenith%5D)


2
[Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BElspeth,%5D+%5BKnight-Errant%5D)


2
[Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BLinvala,%5D+%5BKeeper%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5BSilence%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Dryad+Arbor)


















The main thing you'll notice in Adam's list is the lack of [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). Yes, that's right: one of the format's most defining cards is noticeably absent in deck that contains both white cards and equipment. Why would Adam chose to omit [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)?


"Well, it's just bad." Adam said. He went on to clarify that he was joking and he was really just going for a different strategy.


You see his deck is more concerned with beating the other GW Aggro decks, and even the UW Stone-Blade decks. Another thing you might have noticed is the singleton [Elesh Norn, Grand Cenobite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elesh+Norn%2C+Grand+Cenobite) and [Loyal Retainers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Loyal+Retainers) in the deck. Adam said that the Elesh Norn had been insane for him all weekend!


"So there was this one game where my opponent had a [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes), a Scavenging Ooze, a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), a [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch), a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)*and* an [Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elspeth%2C+Knight-Errant). I played out an Elesh Norn, wiped his board then played a Swords on his Knight. I then swung with my [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) into his Elspeth to kill it! It was insane."


The deck also has several ways to *get* an Elesh Norn into play, including the one-of [Gaea's Cradle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Cradle)! He can search that up with a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary), Search for a Knight with a Shaman, or even search for a [Loyal Retainers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Loyal+Retainers) by *discarding* the Elesh Norn!


Another game Adam mentioned was where he had a [Gaea's Cradle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Cradle) in play and ended up removing his opponent's entire graveyard in two turn with Scavenging Ooze!


When asked what the deck's bad matchups might be, Adam informed that he had been out of the country for a while so he wasn't really sure. "Combo, maybe?" Even then, the Thalias seem like they might put a hurting on his combo opponents.


Adam Cai has been tearing up the event with a mere one loss, and he doesn't seem to show any signs of stopping! Could this be the latest evolution of GW Aggro? Hopefully we'll see in a few short hours!




Sunday, 11:42 a.m. – Day 2 Metagame Breakdown
---------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

So here's a quick breakdown of the decks that made Day 2:




|  |
| --- |
| UW Stone Blade – 22 |
| GW Stone Blade – 22 |
| Canadian Threshold – 15 |
| High Tide – 9 |
| Dredge – 9 |
| Bant Stone Blade – 8 |
| Ad Nauseum Tendrils – 5 |
| Belcher – 5 |
| Esper Stone Blade – 5 |
| Reanimator – 4 |
| Red Deck Wins – 4 |
| UR Delver – 4 |
| Zoo – 4 |
| Elves – 3 |
| Hive Mind – 3 |
| 43 Lands – 2 |
| BUG Control – 2 |
| RUG No Threshold – 2 |
| Show and Tell – 2 |
| Sneak and Tell – 2 |
| Team America – 2 |
| Tezzeret Affinity – 2 |
| Thopter Sword – 2 |
| White Weenie Stone Blade – 2 |
| Affinity – 1 |
| Aggro Loam – 1 |
| Budget Bant – 1 |
| BW Tokens – 1 |
| Dark Aggro Loam – 1 |
| Dream Halls – 1 |
| Enchantress – 1 |
| Goblins – 1 |
| GW Stone Blade w/ Punishing Fire – 1 |
| Merfolk – 1 |
| Monoblack Control – 1 |
| Naya Fire Control – 1 |
| Painted Stone – 1 |
| The Rock – 1 |
| StifleNaut – 1 |
| Tezzeret Thopter Sword – 1 |
| UB Delver – 1 |

As expected from our 20/20 *Visions* yesterday, the three most represented decks are GW Stone Blade, UW Stone blade, and Canadian Threshold, making up over a third of the field. These decks are brutally efficient at dispatching opponents and pack just enough disruption to provide a problem for the myriad of combo decks in the field. Speaking of the myriad of combo decks, following after the big three are an assortment of the bigger combo decks in the field. Decks like [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide), which Michael Bernat used to go undefeated on Day 1, and perennial powers like Dredge, Ad Nauseum Tendrils, and Belcher are all well represented in Day 2, though clearly not to the degree of the big three. Past that, the diversity of Legacy makes itself apparent, with 26 different decks only having one or two representations in the field. It really is anything goes here at Grand Prix Indianapolis, and, if this field is any indicator, anyone has a chance to win.




Sunday, 11:42 a.m. – Day 2 Metagame Breakdown
---------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

Ding! Round 11...


This was the marquee matchup that had really come to define what we've seen from Legacy this weekend, and it happened to occur between the last two 10-0 players: Jason Ford with Canadian Threshold against Tom Martell and his Esper Stone Blade deck. Both decks are variations on previous powerhouses with some new additions to push them over the edge in Legacy. Ford's Canadian threshold deck has its roots in the threshold decks of old, using cheap cantrips to fill the graveyard and provide a constant stream of threats and a stream of burn to both clear the way and finish opponents off. The newest addition to the deck is [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), who flips on



![Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Stoneforge+Mystic)

command thanks to [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), providing an incredibly efficient three-powered attacker. Martell's Esper Stone Blade is the most recent descendant of the [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) Blade decks that terrorized Standard for what seemed like an eternity. This deck uses [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) to snag a quick piece of equipment and then slaps it on a cheap creature to take control of the game. It backs this plan up with various control elements, from [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). The most recent addition to *this* deck is the multi-format all-star: [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls). This card replaces the [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s of old and provides an incredibly cheap, very versatile string of creatures.

Martell was on the play for game 1, opening with a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) to see the opener that Ford had kept. As Ford laid his hand on the table, Martell let out a "Jeez...[Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt) main..." In addition to the removal spell, Martell saw [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour), [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose), [Wooded Foothills](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wooded+Foothills), and [Tropical Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tropical+Island). Martell wasted no time in taking Ford's only pressure: the [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose).


Ford opened his game with a [Tropical Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tropical+Island) and an obviously freshly drawn [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), and kept the cards on top of his deck, clearly liking what he saw. Martell followed suit with a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) of his own, really giving the card its namesake, thinking for a minute before keeping his on top as well. Ford made his first creature of the match, a [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) that was sure to flip on the following turn thanks to [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)'s stacking ability.


Martell cracked a [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) on his turn, and Ford asked him what he was searching out.


"Just the prettiest [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) in the world," Martell responded with a dreamy quality to his voice.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Rd%2011%20Island.JPG)
*The Prettiest [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) in the World.* 

Being a Euro Italy [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island), I was forced to agree. After putting it into play, he made a [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), providing a pair of blockers to stop the Delver, though he knew they wouldn't last long. True to form, Ford flipped his Delver, revealing a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and used the [Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt) to clear away both creatures. The newly-transformed [Insectile Aberration](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Insectile+Aberration) flipped, attacking Martell for three. Martell wanted to see what he was up against, aiming an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) at Ford's hand, taking [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), Ford's only card other than the [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). He soon stripped that from Ford, who had to cast it to stop Martell from flashing back [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls).


During Ford's upkeep, Martell used an [Intuition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intuition) to fetch three more copies of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls). Playing it in ford's upkeep like that forced Ford to use mana to stop it on his turn, which would neuter any possible plays he might have. Ford had nothing and let it resolve. His attack dropped Martell to 6, but it looked like Martell would soon gain control. Sure enough, Martell spent his turn flashing back two copies of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), creating four tokens in the process. Ford wasted no time in attacking into them, and Martell had to think about his blocks. He was definitely blocking the Aberration, but if he only blocked with two and Ford had a removal spell, it would blow him out and leave the Aberration alive. In the end, he realized that any burn would most likely be aimed at his head at that point and blocked with two tokens. Ford indeed let the Aberration die and passed the turn.


On his turn, Martell began to try to reestablish himself. He used a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to replay [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), to which Ford responded with [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), dropping Martel to 3. The [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Inquisition%2Bof%2BKozilek) revealed [Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt), [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). "Well. That's a pretty big game," Martell said, realizing how difficult his position was. He took the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster and made a big show of putting his [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) off to the side. He then crossed his fingers as he tapped out to play [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte), which would soon be able to gain him the life needed to get out of the Danger Zone. When his deck didn't provide an immediate answer, and realizing that there was no way he could beat a Jitte with counters on it, Ford conceded.


Jason Ford 0 – Tom Martell 1


"That was not the correct [Intuition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intuition). As soon as I cast it, I was like, 'That was so dumb...' The right [Intuition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intuition) was [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares). Then I can Swords the Aberration and stay at nine, which is enough life to find something to do later. I had the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster in my hand, too, so I could have always just recast [Intuition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intuition) at some point for the [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls). I even represented the swords to Plowshares, but why didn't I just *get* the Swords?"



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Rd%2011%20Ford.JPG)
*Jason Ford* 

Game 2 started a little slow from Ford considering that he has eight creatures in his deck that can be played for one mana, as well as [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), and [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour). All he did was play a [Volcanic Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Island) and pass the turn. Martell didn't wait, though, playing a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) of his own off of the "prettiest [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) in the world," keeping his cards on top. Ford got back onto the board with a 2/3 [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) which wasn't long for this world. After drawing the second of the cards he wanted from the [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), Martell washed his library with a [Marsh Flats](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Marsh+Flats), grabbing a [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) to cast [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) to rid himself of the Goyf.


Ford found additional pressure on the next turn, [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ing into a [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) that was leagues away from threshold. He also played a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), which Martell had been careful to play around thus far, fetching only basic lands. That trend continued on the following turn as he played a [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp) before recruiting [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), adding a potentially devastating [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) to his arsenal. For wasted no time in frying the Mystic with a [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), to which Martell responded with a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). When the dust settled, the Mystic was dead, and Ford had his second card in his graveyard.


Martell tried to make a second [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) on the next turn, but ford had a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) to stop it. Martell was less than pleased, playfully chiding ford for being a jerk. Then, like a true hypocrite, Martel played a [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) to block Ford's path. At the end of Martell's turn, Ford tried to get something going with a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) into a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), but Martell stopped him with a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce). Ford tried a second [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) on his next turn, but his Canadian Threshold deck was finding it difficult to get into threshold. He simply passed the turn with only three cards in his graveyard.


Martell began to attack with his [Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit)s. The first two dropped Ford back to 20, and two more joined the team after he flashed it back. Things didn't look great for Ford. He did inch himself closer to a better position with a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) into a [Wooded Foothills](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wooded+Foothills), putting him very close to threshold, but Martell turned the tables on him once again. Ford had a [Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt) stripped away from him when Martell cast [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek). Ford chose not to attack because he had five mana up and his last card in hand was a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). He used it soon after when Martell tried to make another [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). Martell's troops attacked, putting Ford to 15. During Martell's upkeep, Ford forced him to pop his [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta) by using [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) on it, putting himself into threshold. Still in his upkeep, another [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) took the fetched [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea) in the graveyard. After drawing, Martell used his remaining four lands to play a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). Jace fatesealed Ford, putting the card on the bottom, and Martell passed the turn.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Rd%2011%20Martell.JPG)
*Tom Martell* 

Ford appeared to be done. He drew his new card and did nothing. Martell kept ticking Jace up, putting yet another card on the bottom of ford's deck. On top of that, he played a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to flash back [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder). Remember that he still hadn't played the [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) he fetched up earlier. Ford started attacking Jace, but Martell had enough [Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit)s from his [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) to kill the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster and chump the Mongoose. When he added another set of [Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit)s with another [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), the end of the game was simply going through the motions. Ford twitched for a few more turns before finally picking up his cards and shaking his hand. Tom Martell now sits atop the standings of Grand Prix Indianapolis 2012, a perfect 11-0.


Jason Ford 0 – Tom Martell 2




Sunday, 12:32 p.m. – Deck Tech: Esper Stone Blade with Tom Martell
------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

Three decks have risen to prominence in this Grand Prix Indianapolis Legacy field: Canadian Threshold, GW Stone Blade, and UW Stone Blade. Despite these decks showing up in force, the man who managed to make it to 11-0 isn't playing any of them. Not exactly.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Deck%20Tech%20Martell.JPG)
*Tom Martell* 

Tom Martell's Esper Stone Blade is definitely a variation on the UW Stone Blade decks that are seemingly everywhere this weekend, but the differences between the two decks really put his deck into a category of its own. Here is his list:







#### Tom Martell Esper Stone Blade – 11-0


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)





[Decklist](#none)
[Stats](#none)
[Sample Hand](#none)





Sort by:
OverviewColorCostRarity




##### Planeswalker (3)



3
[Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BJace,%5D+%5Bthe%5D+%5BMind%5D+%5BSculptor%5D)

1
[Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSword%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5BFeast%5D+%5Band%5D+%5BFamine%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Flooded+Strand)


















When asked why he chose this version of the deck as opposed to the standard UW build that many of the top players in the tournament seem to be running, he had one thing on his mind.


"[Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) is really good. Think of it like this: [Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elspeth%2C+Knight-Errant) is a good card in the traditional UW Stone Blade decks. She takes four turns to do what I can do with this deck in one with [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) and for the same cost. This deck is a lot like [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Squadron%2BHawk) Blade, but rather than spending eight mana on a full set of [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk)s, I have a squad for four mana and only one card."


[Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) has really become a multi-format all-star. It was the breakout card of Grand Prix Kobe 2012, a *Dark Ascension* Limited tournament. It also made its presence felt strongly at the Standard Grand Prix Baltimore a week later, once again making the Top 5 Cards of the weekend. And I Martell's performance is anything to go by, it's likely to be a Top 5 card of this weekend as well. One of the main reasons that Martell described it as "really good" stems from its ability to *take* control, not wait for a chance to do so.


"[Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) allows you to take the control route, but you can go really aggressive with the tokens. If you get two copies of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls), you can even out race a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) with them. At some point, you can just start leaving one back to block and completely dominate the race."


Despite feeling strongly about this deck, many of Martell's teammates opted for the traditional UW deck, a decision he firmly disagrees with.


"I asked Josh Utter-Leyton why he was playing UW instead of this deck. He said he'd rather have [Counterspell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterspell)s than [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) and [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), and I completely disagree. I'd rather be proactive and know what's in their hand. Having perfect information is very powerful in this format. I want to know that I can run my [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull)s out there without fear of a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce). When each spell is so much good, like in Legacy, getting one countered can be devastating."


One of the moments of the weekend that was very informative in my mind came from a booth interview with Patrick Sullivan. He talked about one of the hardest skills to learn in **Magic**: the ability to recognize what phase in the game you are at, be it aggression, defense, or card advantage, and then adopt the proper role. Martell pointed out that the versatility of this deck allows it to play all of those roles very well, as switch between them with ease.


"[Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) is one of those cards that plays really well in every phase. For example, in the last game, after [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Inquisition%2Bof%2BKozilek)ing Jason and taking his [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose), I put him in a situation where I could choose which of my threats I most wanted to resolve, and then force him to react the way that I wanted, eventually resolving my [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) and going for the throat. That's a very proactive stance where I get to be the aggressive deck, even though it may not look like it on the surface. Then, in the next game, I used [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) as a temporary wall of creatures, providing myself enough time to get enough control of the game that I could switch to offense. In that game, I got to use [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) both as defense, preventing him from attacking effectively; card advantage, since I was able to tie up multiple cards of his for the cost of only one card; and eventually aggression, when I got to start attacking. [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) is another of those versatile cards that can serve as both a blocker, attacker, and obvious source of advantage."


With his more proactive bent on the format, Martell seems perfectly matched with a deck that allows him to play the control decks he loves, but be able to directly impact the way the games he plays go, rather than being forced to react as most controlling decks do. The addition of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) to the deck provides it an incredible amount of mileage and only takes up four slots in the deck. While it may not seem like much of a difference from the UW version of the deck, Martell is right on the money when he discusses the difference between this version's ability to be proactive as opposed to reactive, and how well perfect information can be used to his advantage. I don't want to call his deck the better version, because I believe that the deck plays differently enough that I consider it a deck unto itself.

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Wasteland)


















While Luis is a new name to no one, Nate Connor is relatively newer to the Sunday stage. "I feel left out; I'm the only one without a ChannelFireball shirt!" Nate joked.


### Game 1


Both players shuffled up and Luis decided to go to six almost immediately. He kept his six and led off with a [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Rd%2012%20Nate%20Connor.JPG)
*Nathan Connor* 

Nate cast a [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) and revealed a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), an [Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elspeth%2C+Knight-Errant), a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) and a land from Luis' hand. He then played a [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond) and cast a [Rite of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rite+of+Flame) which Luis countered by Luis, removing the [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) from his hand. Luis played a [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand), found a [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra), and played a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) for no value simply to get the beats in. On his next turn he dropped a [Crucible of Worlds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crucible+of+Worlds) then passed back the turn. Nate [Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Probe)d again revealing the remaining Elspeth in Luis' hand.


Luis drew a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and cast it immediately, sending two cards to the top before playing a [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) that promptly shuffled them back into the deck. During Nate's Draw Step he got [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique)'d by Luis revealing an [Elvish Spirit Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Spirit+Guide), two Charbelcher, a [Desperate Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ritual), a [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox) and a [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall). Luis decides to take the [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall) and Nate drew his card. Luis played the same [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) again courtesy of the Crucible, played an Elspeth, then attacked Nate down to four life after pumping with Elspeth.


Nate played a [Land Grant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Grant), revealed no lands, then grabbed his lone [Taiga](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Taiga). He played [Rite of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rite+of+Flame) for two mana, then the [Desperate Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ritual), then cast his Belcher. He then activated it with his [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond). Luis took the opportunity to look at Nate's deck, but they were still on to game two.


Nate Connor 1, Luis Scott-Vargas 0


### Game 2


Nate looks at the clock between rounds. "Yeah, I got time," he says, noticing a mere nine minutes have passed since the beginning of the round. "Maybe I'll have time to get to Starbucks!"


"You know how I playtest this match up?" he asked. "I sleep!"


The banter was friendly and casual but there was money and glory on the line this late in the event. Luis would be on the play this game and led off with [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn). Nate would once again lead with a [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond), but also a [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal) and a [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall). He would then sacrifice the [Tinder Wall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinder+Wall) to play a [Rite of Flame](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rite+of+Flame) for a total of three mana. A seething song would follow, which ate a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) from Luis.


Luis got another turn, but a mere [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra) was all that came. It was land go for Luis and simply a "go" from Nate for a few turns. An [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) would come down for Luis targeting the only permanent in play: Nate's [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond). A [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) as Luis' sixth land meant he could finally press some advantage over Nate despite an otherwise empty board.



![Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Batterskull)

Nate discarded a Charbelcher and passed the turn. Nate then drew a [Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Probe), cast it and Luis revealed two lands and a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). With the coast clear, Nate played a [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal), [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox), and a [Desperate Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ritual), to which Luis used his one [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster to recast his [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). Luis hit a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), attacked for two with the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster, then cast a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) and a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) would join his hand. Luis also drew a Clique and hit Nate on his draw step. He revealed two Charbelchers, a [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish), a [Seething Song](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seething+Song), and a [Desperate Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Desperate+Ritual). Luis went into the tank before deciding to take the seething song. Luis would bounce his Clique with his [Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) at the end of Nate's turn, as he kept pressing his advantage with the [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). The next turn repeated and Nate revealed the [Simian Spirit Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simian+Spirit+Guide) and the second [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish) which he had drawn since the last turn. This time Luis chose the [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish),


The game went like this for a couple more turn before Luis ran out a Jace. He used the +2 ability to Fateseal Nate, shipping a [Pyretic Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyretic+Ritual) to the bottom of his deck. Nate dropped to a mere six life, and the game was looking close. But Nate had a ton of mana in various forms, which allowed him to cast a [Burning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning+Wish) for a [Diminishing Returns](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diminishing+Returns) in his sideboard!


With the [Diminishing Returns](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diminishing+Returns) having resolved, Nate looked at his hand, and with no Charbelcher he had no choice but to scoop 'em up.


Nate Connor 1, Luis Scott-Vargas 1


### Game 3


With Nate having the choice to play, he was at a slight advantage in this matchup. He would keep his initial seven, while Luis went down to six. In this matchup it isn't how many cards you have so much as which cards you have in hand. Luis looked at his new six with disappointment as he sent those back as well. Five...would also not do, so it was off to four cards and the hope of a brighter hand. Luis ended up keeping a hand of [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta), and [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare), which Nate saw from a [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe). Luis found a [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) and was still in the game after casting a turn two Stoneforge!


He found another land in the form of [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), and he put a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) into play at Nate's End step. He swung for seven with the Factory, the [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) and the [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic), dropping Nate to 11 and the initial two damage from the [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe). Luis swung for another seven with the whole team, dropping Nate to four and at that point the game was actually over! Luis manages to win an insane game after mulling to a mere four cards!


Nate Connor 1, Luis Scott-Vargas 2




Sunday, 1:19 p.m. – Tech Deck: Charbelcher with Nathan Connor
-------------------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

Nathan Connor is a casual player at heart. He mentioned this multiple times as he described his deck with utter glee. The deck in question was one of the more well known combo decks in the format: 'Belcher, titled after its namesake card, Charbelcher!



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/Charbelcher.JPG)
*Nathan Connor's Charbelcher Deck.* 

He had a lot of things to say about the deck, so let's display what he's working with.

##### Mythic (4)



4
[Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BLion%5D+%5BEye%5D+%5BDiamond%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Taiga)


















I asked him what his worst matchup was and his response? "[Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)." Yes, the card. Pretty much any deck that runs [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) will give him some trouble, but even then, he says he's played against 10 [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) decks today and he's only lost to three. Either his opponent's are doing something wrong, or he's getting very lucky!


It could be a little of both, as he shows us. "I was in a game where I probed my opponent and saw he had a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). I said, 'okay.' I go [Chrome Mox](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chrome+Mox). He says okay. I go [Lotus Petal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Petal). He says okay. I remove two [Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit) Guides from my hand and mak eight goblins! He sits there and says, 'Well, huh.' And he had the [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)!"



![Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gitaxian+Probe)

Plays like this are par for the deck. It has several ways to win a game and it's hard to prevent them all from occurring. Nate mentioned he cut the [Manamorphose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Manamorphose) since it would often get countered leaving him with no mana and not drawing a card. He has been much happier with the inclusion of [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) which no one counters, it gives him information, and he gets to draw his card. He also made sure to cut a single [Land Grant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Land+Grant). "Having two in your hand at any time is just the worst!" he said.


There are quite a few combo decks in Legacy and Charbelcher can hang with the best of them. As the only deck in Legacy that gets by with only one land in the entire 75 cards, it's definitely a breed of its own!




Round 13 Feature Match - Lewis Laskin vs. Steve Rubin
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

This round presented an opportunity to showcase a couple of unique talents and a unique deck. Lewis Laskin, from Washington DC, is playing a very cool BUG Control deck that is well tailored for the format. His opponent, Steve Rubin, from Pittsburgh, managed to take a more standard deck, UW Stone Blade, to a perfect 9-0 record yesterday. He's picked up a couple of losses on the day, but is still right in the running to make Top 8 here at Grand Prix Indy. The players chatted for a bit about the paths that had brought them here, including where they came from and what decks they had played. Laskin reveaed that he "hadn't played a real deck all weekend." He seemed a little excited at the prospect of playing one when Rubin told him that he was playing one of those "real decks."


### Game 1


Things started out inauspiciously for Rubin, as he was forced to Mulligan to five cards on the play. He opened with a number of lands, including a pair of [Volcanic Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Island)s that exist purely to cast sideboard cards, and a [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand). Laskin did his own best draw-go impression, breaking face only a couple of times in the early turns of the game for a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) and a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage)-powered [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder). He did use [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to deny Rubin one of his [Volcanic Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Island)s, keeping Rubin on three lands. At the end of one of Laskin's turns, Rubin cracked his [Flooded Strand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flooded+Strand) to grab a basic [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) before firing a [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) at Laskin. The Clique revealed a second [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), two [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce)s, [Innocent Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Innocent+Blood), and [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). Rubin chose to get rid of Jace, but Laskin apparently drew into one, as he tapped to play a second copy o the planeswalker on his next turn. Rubin had [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), removing a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage), and Laskin was once again denied a Jace.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/rd%2013%20Rubin.JPG)
*Steve Rubin*

After losing his Jace, Laskin chose to use [Innocent Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Innocent+Blood) to clear the board, leaving his own [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) as the only creature. Rubin had an answer for that as well, using Sword to Plowshares to remove the animated land. Afterwards, Laskin tried to recruit another planeswalker to his team, this time a [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil), but Rubin went down to one card to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) it, removing a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) he couldn't cast on three lands. Three lands *were* enough to cast a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine), but he had no creatures to equip. Laskin set up a protective guard with a [Pernicious Deed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pernicious+Deed) should Rubin find an attacker, ironically able to kill the pro-green and black giving equipment.


With a flash, Rubin started to try to get some threats down. First, he tried a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). That met [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare). Then he tried another. That, too, met a Snare, this time coming back thanks to a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). When he tried the third one, it did hit the table, fetching him a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull), but Laskin had a [Ghastly Demise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghastly+Demise) to immediately kill the Mystic. Even the Batterskul failed to hit the table, Laskin paying five for a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to stop it. This whole while, Laskin had been beating with a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage). Eventually, a [Creeping Tar Pit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Creeping+Tar+Pit) joined the fun, dropping Rubin to two. When Laskin fired it up for the final attack, Rubin tried to cast a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) the animated lad, but Laskin had a counter for it.


Lewis Laskin 1 – Steve Rubin 0


### Game 2


Despite having only five cards to start with, Rubin had managed to find answers for all but one of Laskin's threats. Unfortunately, that one threat went all the way against him. The first game was classic control-on-control, with each threat being answered in turn by both players. The one threat that wasn't handled ended up deciding the game.


While sideboarding, Rubin noticed that Laskin was staring blankly at his fifteen cards.


"You finally play against a real deck and you don't know how to sideboard" Rubin joked?


With a wide-eyed glance at his sideboard, Laskin just exhaled and said, "I have *no* idea."


Game two started with both players keeping their opening draws, though Laskin quickly started hitting Rubin's hand with a series of [Raven's Crime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raven%27s+Crime)s. Rubin protected some of his cards with a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), using it and [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) to see as many cards as possible. Not wanting the Crime to continue, Rubin used a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) to get rid of Laskin's [Underground Sea](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Underground+Sea), his only black source. It took a few turns before he was able to peel a [Bayou](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bayou), and rather than go back to criminal behaviors, he chose instead a [Pernicious Deed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pernicious+Deed). When he upped his game one more step with a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor), Rubin was ready with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will).


From that point, there were a few machine-gun turns of draw go from both players, neither playing land. This favored Laskin as he had four in play already to Rubin's two. Eventually, Rubin had to start discarding, clearly displeased. Fortunately for him, the immediate net turn finally brought a land, but his new [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) was [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland)ed immediately. Laskin made a [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) on his next turn, but opted not to activate her, revealing that his five cards were "really good." At the end of the turn, Rubin made a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) simply to have an attacker to take out Liliana, but it only got to hit her once before Laskin used Deed for two. Rubin continued to fail to improve his lot and passed the turn.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/rd%2013%20laskin.JPG)
*Lewis Laskin* 

Things finally got a little interesting on the following turn when Laskin aimed an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) at Rubin. In his hand, Laskin saw that he had "all the goods." [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), [Pyroblast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyroblast), [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique), Jace, [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring), [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull), and [Elspeth, Knight-Errant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elspeth%2C+Knight-Errant), make for quite an imposing grip of cards. Laskin chose to take the Clique, which was fortunate, as Rubin immediately drew into another blue source. Unfortunately, this left him unable to play anything in his hand still, and he had to pass the turn. Not wanting Rubin to hide his juice from Liliana, Laskin won a counter war over a measly [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) that Rubin tried to use to get himself into the game.


Liliana went to work on Rubin's hand, crushing it card-by-card as a [Creeping Tar Pit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Creeping+Tar+Pit) and [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) started alternating attacks. Rubin dropped to seven. He managed to stick a couple of [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)s, fetching an [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) and a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine), but Liliana just took some time out of her busy discard schedule to deal with it. To deal with the last one, Laskin used a [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to flash back an [Innocent Blood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Innocent+Blood) to clear the path for his lands, Rubin conceded.


Lewis Laskin 2 – Steve Rubin 0




Sunday, 2:37 p.m. - Deck Tech: BUG Control with Lewis Laskin
------------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price*

As I pored over the decklists today to prepare for the Day 2 metagame breakdown, I made careful note of decks that intrigued me. This was the first time I came across Lewis Laskin's BUG Control deck. I didn't really register anything about it except that it was different. When I see that color combination in Legacy, I always assume it's just Team America, but this didn't have any of the trademark cards at all. In fact, it had almost none of them. Noting nothing more than it being a "different" deck, I moved on. A couple rounds later, Frank Lepore came over to let me know about this cool BUG Control deck that he'd seen Laskin playing, and playing well. This jogged my memory and I went to go snag the decklist and give it a look over. Here it is:

[Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BJace,%5D+%5Bthe%5D+%5BMind%5D+%5BSculptor%5D)
