75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Wasteland)


















At first glance, there honestly wasn't anything that really stood out to me about it. It just seemed to be a collection of cards. They were good cards, sure, but this is Legacy. All of the cards are good. At first glance, I wasn't sure how this deck was going to get there. It had two [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage)s, a handful of planeswalkers, and some man-lands backed up by [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam). It just seemed so *slow* in a format where players can't really afford to be. But despite this, Laskin was winning. I wanted to find out more, so I put him in the feature match area to square off with Steve Rubin, who had taken UW Stone Blade to a 9-0 record on Day 1. As you may have read, Laskin won. More importantly, I got to see the deck in action, and I finally understood.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/dt%20bug.JPG)
*BUG Deck* 

I sat down with Laskin after the match to chat a little about his very unorthodox choice for this weekend.


"Heh, traditionally, I'm a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) player. But I figured Maverick (GW Stone Blade) would be a popular deck for this tournament, and I get far fewer draws with *this* slow deck than I ever would playing [Mother of Runes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mother+of+Runes) mirror matches all weekend. The real reason I wanted to play this deck was because I think all of the cards in the deck, especially [Pernicious Deed](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pernicious+Deed), are really well positioned to be exceptional in the format. People are playing fewer planeswalkers these days, and with [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) being so popular...Deed really takes care of everything."


Despite all of this, I still felt as though the deck was nothing more than a pile of reasonably good cards. I saw flashes of it coming together in the feature math, but Laskin really helped drive home how wrong I was.


"Every card in this deck works together. People are playing a lot of on-for-one threats right now. Maverick is actually one of the only decks that commits multiple threats to the board at a time. So I've got a nice little suite of targeted removal. If I play against those decks that do put more out there for me, like Maverick or Elves, I've got the early removal to hold me over until I can wipe the board clear with [Damnation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Damnation) or Deed. I played against an Elves player earlier who built a massive army up and drew a bunch of cards with [Regal Force](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Regal+Force)...and I wiped them all away with my maindeck [Damnation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Damnation).


I also have these [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek)s which can take out important targets in my opponent's hands, as well as all of these [Counterspell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterspell)s to stop the other important cards I saw there. Eventually, I can just get the game locked up with a [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) or a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). A lot of people told me that Liliana was just bad since people could just burn her off if they didn't have a guy, but they've never played her. If they have a guy, I can play Liliana and [Diabolic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diabolic+Edict) it and they still have to spend a burn spell to finish her. If they don't, I can just add a loyalty as soon as I play her, and then I get the card they discard plus two more if they want to kill her. Either way, I come out ahead. And if I have [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) going with Liliana, it gets even better."


Despite these synergies present in his deck, Laskin does admit that there are a few things that he's realized as the tournament went on.


"Originally, I thought about having two more [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)s in the deck, but you really do need all of the other cards in the deck. It's very tight. You don't want to cut removal spells to add search spells when what you'd be searching for is removal. It's better to just have more spells. I'm not even really that big a fan of the [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)s. They're just too aggressive for this deck. Also, I have been considering cutting the third [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). It's only really good against combo, and there aren't too many people playing it right now. It's another one of those cards that is just better in the aggressive decks."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/dt%20laskin.JPG)
*Lewis Laskin* 

Laskin wasn't the first person to bring that up about [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). A few others that I'd talked to this weekend mentioned that [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) just isn't that great because you really don't want to two-for-one yourself like that in this format. About the only decks that really love having a full complement of the spell are the "aggressive" blue decks: the combo decks. At that point, the whole idea is to have a couple of free counterspells that you can use to protect your combo. It's not about stopping other people's offensive spells; it's about stopping their attempts to stop you. How the times have changed. Despite this though, the ones who were making these comments to me were still playing multiple copies of [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and Laskin sweetly summed up why: "It's still [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)."


"The only real problems this deck has are burn decks, which no one should be playing, and combo decks, which you're weak against, but you can still have game against. The creature decks generally don't stand a chance. I'm really pleased with this deck in this format."


His record shows every reason why he should be.




Sunday, 2:46 p.m. - Quick Hits - What did you play?
---------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

What did you play? If you had to play something other than your deck in the tournament, what would it be?



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/QH%20Brian%20Kibler.JPG)
*Brian Kibler – GW Aggro*

"I wouldn't have played [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). That card I just so bad. I want to be doing more proactive things than that. You're just getting this really expensive equipment that doesn't really do anything. I'd just rather play more [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage)s. Pridemage is insane right now, and I'd actually play a fourth. I like the idea of adding something like [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) to the deck, but it doesn't interact very well with [Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben)"



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/QH%20Tom%20Martell.JPG)
*Tom Martell – Esper Stone-Blade*

"I'd play the same deck, no question. I don't like the [Tower of the Magistrate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tower+of+the+Magistrate) in the deck so I would remove that. I also like what [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) and [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) are capable of, so I played two of each in the main deck."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/QH%20Caleb%20Durward.JPG)
*Caleb Durward – Canadian Threshold*

"I'd definitely play the same deck. I think it's one of the best decks in the format, and it's very well rounded. I had a brew that I was about to play, but it just wasn't putting up the same results; although it was able to reanimate a [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) via a [Haakon, Stromgald Scourge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Haakon%2C+Stromgald+Scourge)! I think my worst matchup is probably the Stone-Blade decks, but I would love to face [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide) since I have [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) and a million one mana spells."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/QH%20Matt%20Costa.JPG)
*Matt Costa – RUG delver (Canadian Threshold)*

"No, the deck is very good. I mean, I don't really play legacy, so up until Friday night I was going to play UW Stone-Blade.


I think [Thought Scour](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Scour) really pushes it over the top, since you can do things you couldn't do with [Mental Note](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Note), like ruin their stacking with a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) if they kept, or milling their threat after Submerging it. I don't really want to face the Esper Stone-Blade lists. I feel like [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) solves a lot of the problems the deck had."



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/QH%20Patrick%20Sullivan.JPG)
*Patrick Sullivan – UR Delver*

"If I didn't play UR Delver, I would have probably played Zoo. The Combo matches are pretty bad. Faster combo decks are pretty hard to deal with, but slower combos are usually a little better. Basically the faster and less interactive their decks are, the worse it is for my deck. I didn't run any counters like the normal UR Delver lists; I just have [Mindbreak Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindbreak+Trap) in the sideboard.




Round 15 Feature Match: One Counter to Rule Them All! – Adam Yurchick vs. Alix Hatfield
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Frank Lepore*

The players casually bantered back and forth before the match discussing various plays and moments throughout their careers. You'd never guess that a Top 8 appearance was resting on the fate of this match!


### Game 1


Adam rolled an eleven, while Alix rolled a ten. Adam led off with...a mulligan. Alix was satisfied with his opener, but Adam has to go down to five. Not the best of starts, but we've seen players come back from much worse.


Eventually Adam was able to keep on five and they were off. Both players led with [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s, and Adam followed with a [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra). Alix attempted a [Merchant Scroll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merchant+Scroll), but Adam said no with a Mana leak. On Adam's turn he proceeded to brainstorm then played a [Polluted Delta](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Polluted+Delta). A land and a pass from Alix and Adam was searching for a [Volcanic Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Island). He drew for his turn then attempted to cast a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor).


"How many cards?" Alix inquired.


"Two," Adam responded.


"It resolves."


Adam passed back the turn after brainstorming with Jace, and Alix attempted to resolve a [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide). It resolved, then he immediately cast a *Time Spiral* with his remaining three lands. Both players shuffled up, drew their new seven, and Alix untapped his four lands that he could tap for eight mana! Alix would then play a [Merchant Scroll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merchant+Scroll) and search out a second [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide), which would allow his [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s to produce three blue mana each when tapped. A [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) from Alix followed by a Candelabra could spell doom for Adam, but the game went on. Alix cast a second [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) followed by a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) which allowed him to dig deeper through his deck to keep the combo in motion. Another *Time Spiral* from Alix virtually guaranteed it. Both players shuffled up and drew another full grip of seven cards.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/RD%2015%20Alix%20Hatfield.JPG)
*Alix Hatfield*

[High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide) number three for Alix meant each of his [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s were now producing four mana each! He cast a [Cunning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cunning+Wish) and Adam inquired about the storm count.


"Storm is...?"


"Eleven," Alix responded.


Alix thought long and hard about what he would search for, before deciding on a [Blue Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blue+Sun%27s+Zenith). Alix then chose to target himself and draw six cards. With two [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s open – a potential eight mana – Adam acknowledged. Alix tapped another [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island), floting three mana, and cast the fourth [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide). Five blue mana per [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) was the count.


Alix cast a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) followed by a brainstorm as he looked for a win condition. He found it in a second [Candelabra of Tawnos](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Candelabra+of+Tawnos). Alix asked Adam if he would concede if he could show Adam the path to victory and Adam agreed. Alix ran through the motions of [Blue Sun's Zenith](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blue+Sun%27s+Zenith)'ing Adam for the remainder of his cards and the game was over.


Alix Hatfield 1, Adam Yurchick 0


### Game 2


"I'll start," Adam noted. Both players kept and Adam led with a [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest). A first turn [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) from Alix was par for the course when most of his deck one mana cantrips. Another land from Adam and it was back and forth. Alix attempted a turn two [Merchant Scroll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merchant+Scroll), but Adam had the ideal counter in the form of a [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare). A [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) from Alix and his deck velocity was off the charts. He played a land then passed the turn to Adam.


Adam cracked two of his fetch lands and attempted to cast a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). In response Alix chose to [Meditate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meditate). Adam then responded by cracking a third fetch land and letting the [Meditate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meditate) resolve. Four cards and a missed turn would be the price Alix paid. Adam [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)ed with Jace before passing the turn...back to himself. He took his second turn which consisted of a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) searching up a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull), and a land.



![High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=High+Tide)

Alix attempted to [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide), which was met with a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce). The [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) was met with a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), but Adam had a second [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) for the [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide). The second [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) was *also* met with a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) from Alix, and the stack grew larger. Adam had the final [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) in the Chain, however. But that's not all! Alix had the Flusterstorm targeting [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), storming for seven copies! The [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide) resolved, prompting a *Time Spiral* from Alix, but Adam had the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster to get back a [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce), essentially negating the entire chain of events!


With Alix very low on cards, things were looking up for Adam as he played another [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). He found a [Sword of Body and Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Body+and+Mind) and attacked Alix down to 16 with the [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster. Alix played a [Merchant Scroll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merchant+Scroll) and Adam responded with a brainstorm to stop it by any means necessary. Adam found the [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare) then cheated into play a [Sword of Body and Mind](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Body+and+Mind). He equipped his [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap)caster after a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) from Jace and entered the red zone. Alix would drop to 11 life while Adam would gain a wolf and mill him ten cards.


Alix went to 10 from his [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn) and drew for his turn. He played a second [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn) and passed the turn After Adam put a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) into play, threatening exactly ten damage, it was on to game three.


Alix Hatfield 1, Adam Yurchick 1


### Game 3


Alix was on the play here which could give him the momentum he needed to take the match. He led with a first turn Candelabra, while Adam had a [Tundra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tundra). Alix cast a ponder following by land. Adam laid a land then passed the turn. Both players were content to build their mana bases in the early game.


Alix cast a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and cracked a [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn) after putting his two cards back on top. Alix cast another [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) on his turn, followed by a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder); he was sculpting the perfect hand. It didn't stop there though, as Alix played a *second* [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)! After Alix had tapped out and passed the turn, Adam responded with a [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique), threatening to ruin Alix's well crafted plans.


Alix revealed two [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), a [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide), a [Cunning Wish](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cunning+Wish), a *Time Spiral*, and a Flusterstorm. Adam let him keep them all and untapped. After crashing for three damage he attempted to cast a [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic). This gave Alix pause, but it ultimately resolved and Adam found a [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull). With little gas in Alix's hand the game was looking good for Adam. Alix cast a [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide), and Adam attempted to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) it. This was met with a [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) by Alix. [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide) resolved and he floated four mana before untapping all three lands with his Candelabra. Alix then cast *Time Spiral* with a mere one blue mana floating when the dust settled.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpind12/RD%2015%20Adam%20Yurchick.JPG)
*Adam Yurchick*

He played a land then attempted to cast a [Meditate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meditate). Adam had the hard counter for it in the form of a [Counterspell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterspell). Alix played a [Pact of Negation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pact+of+Negation) to counter it, but Adam had the [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to target the [Meditate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Meditate) for a second time. Alix then passed the turn, and since time was called during Adam's turn, Adam was turn on turn one. He attacked Alix down to eight life with a Factory and his two creatures, and passed the turn.


Alex untapped, cracked his fetchland and drew his card for the turn...


...which unfortunately meant that Alix had missed his [Pact of Negation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pact+of+Negation) trigger!


As the [Pact of Negation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pact+of+Negation) was not countered on the last turn, and Alix did not pay for it during his upkeep, Adam clinches a Top 8 berth at Grand Prix Indianapolis!


Alix Hatfield 1, Adam Yurchick 2
